Personal story: I got invited after 5+ years of not biking to bike again... Tomorrow. Fearing since my front brakes were blown (hose to master cylinder blew) and my grips melting from sitting out in the sun I brought my bike to my shop to fix (I mean a auto shop has 70% of what I need to fix bikes.)

Yet.) Brake system. Shimano being a reputable I called in to inquire if they had it in stock since online said "maybe."

Called not knowing it was 11:35am I realized they don't open till noon. Left an voicemail and surprisingly, I received a call around 12:30 with the fact I gave them an oddball part number, but asked about a basic brake kit. Guy on the phone offered "we got this kit" and so things were settled. I'm going up to Fremont rather than driving to Santa Cruz.

took "lunch" to drive up to Fremont to this store and was nicely greeted asking what I was looking for, pointed me to the products I needed (with recommended products, but not pushy to sale a specific (potentially higher markup) item. I selected my items and went to the parts/repair area.

"What were you looking for exactly?"

I replied "a Shimano handle and caliper premade"

He replied "oh you called earlier right?"

After that I was handed the item, paid for it and booked back to the shop and rapidly threw it on, bedded the brakes and I'm now ready for our socially distancing trail ride.

Too long, didn't read: no pushy sales people, prices are fair, didn't have any bad vibes, wish they had more variety (but can't blame them totally because the store looked like a target after black Friday haha)
Oh and I didn't really dig into the parts section since there were too many people in that area

Would recommend if it's near you. As for me they luckyly had what I needed in one stop.< /Text>

Our $12 repair covers most wheels but kids bike rear wheels can have training wheels, chain guards, and a coaster brake that all must be disassemble before the wheel can even be removed.  This is why we charge $20.  The $15 was a compromise from the service manager since there were no training wheels.  Once the wheel was removed we discovered that the tire had large tears requiring that it be replaced.  Putting a new tube in a tire like that will result in an immediate failure.  So originally it was $15 for the labor and $7.99 for the tube or $22.99 total.  When we discovered the tire problem you were offered a tube and tire combo for $10 for a total of $25 instead.  At this point we had already done a fair amount of work which needed to be done in order to discover the tears in the tire.  My understanding was you did not not want to pay the $25 to have it fixed with a new tire so the service manager still wanted to charge for the labor performed at that point, then also to put the tire back on the bike and reassemble everything.  I think anger on both sides led to this unfortunate experience.  I'm sorry this didn't work out to your expectations.  Unfortunately the days of bicycle stores being able to give away free labor are gone.  Margin on products is so small now due to the internet that labor can no longer be subsidized by parts sales.  Labor must pay for itself.  We should have explained this first to avoid the conflict in expectations.  Our prices are posted on our web page and are open to the public.  I'm not sure why you were told you must ask for permission to photograph them.  I'll ask the service manager about that."}<//Response>

<user>100025190394579931817</user><review>This shop did the diagnosis for our vehicle emissions monitors not ready issue for a reasonable price.  However, the diagnosis is incorrect.  The shop recommended us to replace the catalytic converter and the front oxygen sensor for over $2300.  Today we took our car to a Toyota dealership for a second opinion.  The dealership made all emissions monitors ready without repairing or replacing any parts.  The tecician at the dealership only did a specific Toyota drive cycle for the car. We were only charged for $155, and the car passed the smog check afterwards.  I will not take my car to this shop again for any services no matter how price competitive this shop is.  I feel that this shop technicians don't have sufficient emissions knowledge and the owner treated us like his money tree.

I want every one to know that before I took my car to this shop, my car with only about 31,600 miles was running like a brand new car.  It did not have any Diagnostic Trouble Codes (DTCs), or any Malfunction Indicator Lights (MIL) on.  Besides, this car did not show any symptoms of a bad catalytic converter or a bad oxygen sensor. < Review>
1999 ford f250 super duty, 4x4 7.3 turbo diesel

I recently had the front axel seals replaced on the above listed vehicle on or about Nov 06, 2018 at ALL LUBE AND TUNE, 521 W. Imperial hwy, La Habra.    After having a disagreement with the cost, they performed the axel seal replacement.  I drove the truck home.  The next day I went to drive truck and noticed the front axels were again leaking and worse. I returned to the shop and explained the truck was leaking and worse.  They put the truck on the rack, looked at it and sprayed it with break cleaner.  The mechanic told me to take it to car wash and wash the axels.  I told the mechanic owner I was leaving to Arizona.  The owner said I would be ok.  On 11/29 or 30 I drove to Arizona, approx 290 miles.  Upon arrival I noticed the wheel wells and parts of the engine compartment covered with an oil substance.  I looked under the truck and found the axels severely leaking.  I went to a local shop and they put the truck on a rack  needless to say oil was dripping from the axels.  They repaired the truck and found the seals were not properly installed.  When I returned to ALL TUNE AND LUBE and explained that I got stuck and had to have the truck fixed, the owner said they would not reimburse me for the repairs.  He told me that I had to go through NAPA but was not provided any paperwork regarding warranty.
I found this shop through Repairpal, saw that they had a pretty good ratings, and saw where the worl is  guaranteed.  Needless to say I am extremely disappointed.<//Review>

< review>
Everyone dreads the inevitable with one's vehicle... that is, a strange noise from beneath the hood, or a never-before-seen light appear in the dash board. In my case, the vehicle didn't start. Dead as a 10-year-old corpse! A cornucopia of free advice came from all directions: "It's the Alternator!" "It's the switch to the Alternator!" All this was dreaded, of course, because of the costs involved.
When I had my Silverado towed to Don's, he said it may only be the battery and, sure enough!, it turned out to simply be the battery in the face of all the bad advice I got.
Honesty is what we dream of when we take our vehicles in for service.  And honesty is what we pay for, as well.
I got both at Don's last week!

< review>
Service was excellent, and sushi was very good.  To the reviewer who said the sushi was warm, the rice is supposed to be warm, not cold and the fish shouldn't be slightly cool, but not cold.

The rice to sashimi (fish) ratio is too much, but I cut the portion of rice in half and ate that with my tempura and shumai.  So keep that in mind.  I'm pretty sure like other places, that you can't take off the fish and leave the rice.  I didn't do it, so I don't know for a fact but its a safe assumption.

Service was outstanding, and the main reason I'm going back.  Food was good, but service made me feel like an old time regular, and they were SUPER busy, too.

Safe bet to go get sushi if you're in the area.  I enjoyed it very much, and food was solid.<//review>

4 stars.

1 star

< Name>
Lowell Harrison<//Name>
< text>
We have had our Vivint system for one year. We're in Oakland, so this review goes to the nearest office location. I wish we had gone with a different provider, but since we bought about $1000 worth of equipment through Vivint, it makes more sense to stick with them. Here is a list of disappointments:
- Camera placement was done thoughtlessly, or at least with very little understanding of the range and radius of the camera view. For example, we can't see the face of someone who is at our front door, and we also can't see someone who is walking closely along the front wall of our house.
- We have had numerous instances of trying to check the video footage of people on the property, only to find that the motion-activated camera did not activate. Other times, we notice that there are hundreds of video clips from a single day of the camera being activated by...nothing at all. The motion-activated feature seems inconsistent. The fact that we may or may not have a record of someone entering the property is a major let-down.
- Our interior motion sensor was installed into the corner between two walls with screws that only pierce into about 1/16" of drywall. The sensor soon fell over when the front door was slammed. We reinstalled it ourselves at a different spot on the wall.
- We had a random vandalism on the house and tried to download the video footage a couple of weeks later. It turns out our system's storage settings had been configured to delete video after a certain number of days. We were pretty sure the technician said we could always retrieve footage from Vivint headquarters. After inquiring, Vivint recalibrated our system to delete after 45 days instead of the original less than two weeks. Why didn't they do this in the first place? It seems like our system was configured based on how the technician was feeling that day, not based on our needs.
- Main display often freezes and glitches while reviewing video footage. For example, when scrolling through a long list of short video clips, it freezes. When fwd/rewinding a video with the tracking icon, the display often freezes. On the plus side, we learned how to restart the device from our Vivint phone app.
- Motion detector often takes up to five seconds to activate when we're home. Other times, it gets activated immediately. The inconsistency is troubling.

I still give three stars because the devices and customer service have served the bare minimum of our needs. However, I would not recommend Vivint because of the sense that they didn't really listen to our needs, didn't install the motion detector and cameras in a thoughtful way, and their main display computer is glitchy.<//text>

< Text>
Staying at hotel one night for fiance to take a 3 hour entrance exam for the Operating Engineers Journeyman Apprenticeship Training Center (located less than half a mile from the Murrieta Inn & Spa) at 7:30 am the following morning.
Even though the hotel it's self was a splurge, I felt he deserved an easy morning on testing day. Being the ever thoughtful gentleman that he is requested I permit him to treat me to dinner at the hotel's restaurant. I've had my fair share of hotel stays encompassing the entire spectrum of quality and type as well as having worked in fine dining during my 20s in Tucson AZ. Although we started our visit less than an hour before closing on a Monday night, THIS WAS BY FAR ONE OF THE TOP 3 BEST TASTING MEALS I HAVE EVER HAD THE PLEASURE OF DINING UPON. Both our meals (his: the filet, farm fresh veggies and mashed potatoes; mine: the salmon, same veggies and crispy fingerling potatoes) were delightful, though his filet was far closer to  well done than the medium well he'd asked for as it was cooked light brown all the way through and had NO pink with the exception of about one square inch on a thicker edge. It was still delicious, tender and every last morsel was savored. He, the ever picky eater (special orders everything plain as possible even at fast food places) and I with my minimal appetite, and spoiled by my years in fine dining, BOTH FINISHED EVERY LAST BITE ON OUR PLATES.

COMPLIMENTS TO THE CHEF. EXCEEDED EXPECTATIONS.< /Text>

Not even worthy of one star. Made an appointment online for a termite inspection.No one from the company called to confirm. Day of appointment, sales person from the Santa Fe Springs office, Edwin, texted to say he was running late but would be there; this was still within the 2-hour window they gave me, annoying, but not unreasonable. When he finally arrives and I show him termite droppings in garage he says those are old, you've had an infestation for a long time, you can tell because the droppings are a dark color. Yes, we know we've had an infestation for awhile, but the garage is actually framed in redwood which makes the droppings a dark color. He proceeds to walk around the house "inspecting" using the flashlight on his phone. He does a cursory "inspection" in the attic, failing to notice we actually have two separate attic spaces due to an addition. He spends 5 minutes walking the perimeter of the house, failing to notice the active infestation we have in the fascia. He never even bothered to go under the house to look for subterranean termites, which we know we have. So after the 20-minute "inspection",  I get the sales pitch which is basically the cost of the tenting and the special spray that causes termites to die when they land on the treated surface (Really? Rolling my eyes). When I say I need to discuss with my partner, and ask for the estimate to be emailed to me, he types some more on his tablet and presents the "special discount price" which my credit card will "guarantee" for 3-days, if I decide to cancel in that time, no problem, my card will not be charged. Trying not to laugh out loud, I again say I need to think about it, and to please send me the estimate. I try to ask him some questions about security during tenting. The patronizing, unprofessional, disrespectful attitude irritates me, but worse, I'm sure many people fall for these sales tactics.  Terminix used to have a great reputation. If you are thinking about using this company, do your research, and carefully consider the other reviews online.< /review>

<user_name>Bill Verdery< /user_name><Rate>1< /Rate><resp>None</resp><Text>You wrote a review for Terminix	3 weeks ago
1.0 star rating 7/2/2018
Another terrible review! Why bother taking time writing? So no one else will use this company.

First, my previous company was bought out by Terminix. This spring on our annual inspection, the inspector, who is really an inexperienced salesman in sheep's clothing, found rat droppings, fresh, in the attic. Not surprising. So I accepted their exclusion service, which was fine. But then they put traps in the attic to remove any rats. They did not check the traps for a month, until I called and asked them to. Surprise, no rats! Great. But I know that they did not remove the traps, and they did not ever come back to check them. So I probably have dead, decaying rats in my attic.

Second, the salesman said they could get rid of my gophers but I needed to add the whole house coverage with an initial cost of $500 plus $100 each quarter. He said that they would not use poison, since we have dogs. However, the technician doing the job said they always use poison. The long and short is, 6 months later, we still are overrun with gophers. And, they know that they are not fixing the problem so they don't bother coming any more.

Repeated calls to the company supervisor are unanswered. When I call in (by the way, the phone service and operators are VERY NICE and cooperative!!), I am promised a call back within two days.
